href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td>\n<div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_apsar" title="Abkhazian apsar">Abkhazian class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">(<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Abkhazia" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Constitution of Abkhazia">Article 6 of the Constitution</a>) guarantees the right to use their mother tongue for all ethnic groups.</li><li value="2">Annulled by Georgia immediately thereafter.</li><li value="3">To establish, retroactively, <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> independence since the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992-1993)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Abkhazia (1992-1993)">1992\xe2\x80\x931993 war</a>.</li><li value="4">5 UN member states recognize Abkhazia\'s independence.</li><li value="5"><i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">De facto</a></i> currency. Several <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_apsar" title="Abkhazian apsar">Abkhazian apsar</a> commemorative coins have been issued. The apsar is on a fixed exchange rate, pegged to the Russian ruble (1 ruble = 0.10 apsar).</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Abkhazia</b> (<small><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Abkhazia-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bd/En-Abkhazia-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Abkhazia-pronunciation.ogg">pronunciation</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>\xc2\xb7<a href="/wiki/File:En-Abkhazia-pronunciation.ogg" title="File:En-Abkhazia-pronunciation.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></small> <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhazian language">Abkhazian</a>: <span lang="ab">\xd0\x90\xd2\xa7\xd1\x81\xd0\xbd\xd1\x8b\xcc\x81</span>, <small><abbr title="transliteration">translit.</abbr>&#160;</small><i lang="ab-Latn" title="Abkhazian-language transliteration">Apsny</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ap\xca\xb0s\xcb\x88n\xc9\xa8]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>&#58; <span lang="ka" title="Georgian language text">\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\xa4\xe1\x83\xae\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\x96\xe1\x83\x94\xe1\x83\x97\xe1\x83\x98</span> <i><i lang="ka-Latn" title="Georgian-language transliteration">Apxazeti</i></i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Georgian" title="Help:IPA/Georgian">[\xc9\x91p\xca\xb0x\xc9\x91z\xc9\x9bt\xca\xb0i]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>&#58; <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\x90\xd0\xb1\xd1\x85\xd0\xb0\xcc\x81\xd0\xb7\xd0\xb8\xd1\x8f</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">tr.</a></small> <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian language text">Abh\xc3\xa1zija</i>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">[\xc9\x90\xcb\x88pxaz\xca\xb2\xc9\xaaj\xc9\x99]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Abkhazia</b>, is a de facto and partially recognized <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> on the eastern coast of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, south of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">Greater Caucasus</a> mountains, in northwestern Georgia. It covers 8,660 square kilometres (3,340&#160;sq&#160;mi) and has a population of around 240,000. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">Sukhumi</a>. The separatist Abkhazian polity, formally the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_Abkhazia" title="Government of the Republic of Abkhazia">Republic of Abkhazia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Faultlines_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faultlines-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clogg_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clogg-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Karagiannis_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karagiannis-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Olympics_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympics-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> is <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">recognised as a state</a> by <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. While Georgia lacks control over Abkhazia, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Georgia_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Georgia (country)">Georgian government</a> and most <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> member states legally consider Abkhazia part of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, whose constitution designates the area as the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Autonomous_Republic_of_Abkhazia" title="Government of the Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia">Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia</a>.\n</p><p>The status of Abkhazia is a central issue of the <a href="/wiki/Georgian%E2%80%93Abkhazian_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhazian conflict">Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhazian conflict</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgia%E2%80%93Russia_relations" title="Georgia\xe2\x80\x93Russia relations">Georgia\xe2\x80\x93Russia relations</a>. The region enjoyed <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_ASSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz ASSR">autonomy</a> within <a href="/wiki/Georgian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian SSR">Soviet Georgia</a> at the time when the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Soviet Union began to disintegrate</a> in the late 1980s. Simmering ethnic tensions between the <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz people">Abkhaz</a>\xe2\x80\x94the region\'s <a href="/wiki/Titular_nation" title="Titular nation">"titular ethnicity"</a>\xe2\x80\x94and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian people">Georgians</a>\xe2\x80\x94the largest single ethnic group at that time\xe2\x80\x94culminated in the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992%E2%80%931993)" title="War in Abkhazia (1992\xe2\x80\x931993)">1992\xe2\x80\x931993 War in Abkhazia</a> which resulted in Georgia\'s loss of control of most of Abkhazia, the <i>de facto</i> independence of Abkhazia, and the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Georgians_in_Abkhazia" title="Ethnic cleansing of Georgians in Abkhazia">ethnic cleansing of Georgians</a> from Abkhazia. Despite the <a href="/wiki/Agreement_on_a_Cease-fire_and_Separation_of_Forces" title="Agreement on a Cease-fire and Separation of Forces">1994 ceasefire agreement</a> and years of negotiations, the dispute remains unresolved. The long-term presence of a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Observer_Mission_in_Georgia" title="United Nations Observer Mission in Georgia">United Nations Observer Mission</a> and a Russian-led <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS) peacekeeping force failed to prevent the flare-up of violence on several occasions. In August 2008, Abkhaz forces fought against Georgian forces during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War" title="Russo-Georgian War">Russo-Georgian War</a>, which led to the formal recognition of Abkhazia by Russia, the annulment of the 1994 ceasefire agreement, and the termination of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> mission. On 28 August 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Georgia" title="Parliament of Georgia">Parliament of Georgia</a> declared Abkhazia a <a href="/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia" title="Occupied territories of Georgia">Russian-occupied territory</a>, a stance supported by the vast majority of the international community.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 <span class="toctext">Geography and climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Politics_and_government"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Politics and government</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Autonomous_Republic_of_Abkhazia"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Administrative_divisions"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Administrative divisions</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Military"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Military</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Language"><span of Russian nationality</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-30"><a href="#Issue_of_ethnic_Georgians"><span class="tocnumber">8.5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Issue of ethnic Georgians</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Abkhazians call their homeland <span lang="ab" title="Abkhazian language text">\xd0\x90\xd2\xa7\xd1\x81\xd0\xbd\xd1\x8b</span> (<i><i lang="ab-Latn" title="Abkhazian-language transliteration">Apsny</i></i>, <i><i lang="ab-Latn" title="Abkhazian-language transliteration">A\xe1\xb9\x97sny</i></i>), <a href="/wiki/Popular_etymology" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular etymology">popularly etymologised</a> as "a land/country of the soul",<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> yet literally meaning "a country of mortals (mortal beings)".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It possibly first appeared in the seventh century in an Armenian text as <i>Psin(oun)</i>, perhaps referring to the historical <a href="/wiki/Apsilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Apsilian">Apsilians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hewitt2013_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hewitt2013-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The state is formally designated as the "Republic of Abkhazia" or "Apsny".<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Russian <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\x90\xd0\xb1\xd1\x85\xd0\xb0\xd0\xb7\xd0\xb8\xd1\x8f</span> (<i><i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language transliteration">Abkhazia</i></i>) is adapted from the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a> <span lang="ka" title="Georgian language text">\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\xa4\xe1\x83\xae\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\x96\xe1\x83\x94\xe1\x83\x97\xe1\x83\x98</span> (<i><i lang="ka-Latn" title="Georgian-language transliteration">Apkhazeti</i></i>). In <a href="/wiki/Mingrelian_language" title="Mingrelian language">Mingrelian</a>, Abkhazia is known as <span lang="xmf" title="Mingrelian language text">\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\x91\xe1\x83\x9f\xe1\x83\xa3\xe1\x83\x90</span> (<i><i lang="xmf-Latn" title="Mingrelian-language transliteration">Abzhua</i></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> or <span lang="xmf" title="Mingrelian language text">\xe1\x83\xa1\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\xa4\xe1\x83\xae\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\x96\xe1\x83\x9d</span> (<i><i lang="xmf-Latn" title="Mingrelian-language transliteration">saapkhazo</i></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Abkhazia\'s names in Western languages derived directly from the Russian form: Abkhazie in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>; Abkhazien in Danish; Abchasien in German; Abch\xc3\xa1zie in <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>; Abchazi\xc3\xab in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>; Abcasia in <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>; Abjasia in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>; and Abc\xc3\xa1zia in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Abkhazia" title="History of Abkhazia">History of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Between the 9th and 6th centuries BC, the territory of modern Abkhazia was part of the ancient Georgian kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Colchis" title="Colchis">Colchis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> This kingdom was subsequently absorbed in 63 BC into the <a href="/wiki/Egrisi" class="mw-redirect" title="Egrisi">Kingdom of Lazica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1000 and 550 BC, the Greeks established trade colonies along the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> coast of present-day Abkhazia, in particular at <a href="/wiki/Pitsunda" title="Pitsunda">Pitiunt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">Dioscurias</a>, which was to become the capital of modern-day Abkhazia, encountering local warlike tribes whom they dubbed <a href="/wiki/Heniochi" title="Heniochi">Heniochi</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Classical authors described various peoples living in the region and the great multitude of languages they spoke.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arrian" title="Arrian">Arrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> have given accounts of the <a href="/wiki/Abasgoi" title="Abasgoi">Abasgoi</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mushki#Moschoi" title="Mushki">Moschoi</a><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> peoples somewhere in modern Abkhazia on the eastern shore of the Black Sea.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> conquered Egrisi in the 1st century AD and ruled it until the 4th century, following which it regained a measure of independence, but remained within the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>\'s sphere of influence. Although the exact time when the population of the region of Abkhazia was converted to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> has not been determined, it is known that the Metropolitan of <a href="/wiki/Pityus" class="mw-redirect" title="Pityus">Pityus</a> participated in the First Ecumenical Council in 325 in <a href="/wiki/First_Council_of_Nicaea" title="First Council of Nicaea">Nicaea</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Around the mid 6th century AD, the Byzantines and the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Sassanid_Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sassanid Persia">Sassanid Persia</a> fought for supremacy over Abkhazia for 20 years, a conflict known as the <a href="/wiki/Lazic_War" title="Lazic War">Lazic War</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg/220px-Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg.png" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg/330px-Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg/440px-Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1155" data-file-height="898" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus_1124_AC_en_alt.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Kingdom of Abkhazia was united through dynastic succession with the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Kingdom of Georgia</a> in 1008 when Bagrat II of Abkhazia became <a href="/wiki/Bagrat_III_of_Georgia" title="Bagrat III of Georgia">Bagrat III of Georgia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Abkhazia, or Abasgia in classic sources, formerly part of Colchis and later of Lazica until the late 690s, was a <a href="/wiki/Princedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Princedom">princedom</a> under <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine empire">Byzantine</a> authority. <a href="/wiki/Anacopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Anacopia">Anacopia</a> was the princedom\'s capital. The country was mostly Christian, with the archbishop\'s seat in Pityus.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> An Arab incursion into Abkhazia led by <a href="/wiki/Marwan_II" title="Marwan II">Marwan II</a>, was repelled by <a href="/wiki/Leon_I_of_Abkhazia" title="Leon I of Abkhazia">Leon I</a> jointly with his Lazic and <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Iberia" title="Principality of Iberia">Iberian</a> allies in 736.\n</p><p>After acquiring Lazica  via a dynastic union in the 780s<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Abkhazia" title="Kingdom of Abkhazia">Kingdom of Abkhazia</a> was established and became a dominant power in western <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>. During this period the Georgian language replaced <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> as the language of literacy and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The western Georgian kingdom flourished between 850 and 950 when it annexed significant parts of central Georgia. A period of unrest ensued, which ended as Abkhazia and eastern Georgian states were <a href="/wiki/Unified_Georgian_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Georgian Kingdom">unified</a> under a single <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Georgian monarchy</a>, ruled by <a href="/wiki/Bagrat_III_of_Georgia" title="Bagrat III of Georgia">King Bagrat III</a> (who was buried in the <a href="/wiki/Bedia_Cathedral" title="Bedia Cathedral">Monastery of Bedia</a> in eastern Abkhazia) at the end of the 10th century and the beginning of the 11th century. In 12th century, king <a href="/wiki/David_IV_of_Georgia" title="David IV of Georgia">David the Builder</a> appointed the son of <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">shah</a> <a href="/wiki/Shirvan" title="Shirvan">Shirvan</a> Otago as an <a href="/wiki/Eristavi" title="Eristavi">Eristavi</a> of Abkhazia, who later became the founder of <a href="/wiki/House_of_Shervashidze" title="House of Shervashidze">House of Shervashidze</a> (also known as Sharvashidze, or Chachba). In the 1240s, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongols</a> divided Georgia into eight military-administrative sectors (dumans), the territory of contemporary Abkhazia formed part of the duman administered by <a href="/wiki/Tsotne_Dadiani" title="Tsotne Dadiani">Tsotne Dadiani</a>.\n</p><p>In the 16th century, after the break-up of the Georgian Kingdom into small kingdoms and principalities, <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Abkhazia" title="Principality of Abkhazia">Principality of Abkhazia</a> (nominally a vassal of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Imereti" title="Kingdom of Imereti">Kingdom of Imereti</a>) emerged, ruled by the Shervashidze dynasty.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1570s, when the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">Ottoman navy</a> occupied the fort of <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">Tskhumi</a>, Abkhazia came under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and Islam. Under <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> rule, the majority of Abkhaz elite converted to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. The principality retained a degree of autonomy. Georgia signed a treaty with Russia for protection against the Ottoman Empire in 1773 and was seemingly absorbed, while Abkhazia sought protection from <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> in 1801, but was declared as "an autonomous principality" by the Russians in 1810.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Russia then annexed Abkhazia in 1864, and Abkhaz resistance was quashed as the Russians deported Muslim Abkhaz to Ottoman territories.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Within_the_Russian_Empire">Within the Russian Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Within the Russian Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg/220px-Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg/330px-Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg/440px-Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="567" data-file-height="418" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhazia_%26_Samurzakan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The borders of the <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi_District_(Russian_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sukhumi District (Russian Empire)">Sukhumi District</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kutaisi_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Kutaisi Governorate">Kutaisi Governorate</a> in 1899 when Abkhazia was part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the beginning of the 19th century, while the Russians and Ottomans were vying for control of the region, the rulers of Abkhazia shifted back and forth across the religious divide.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The first attempt to enter into relations with Russia was made by <a href="/wiki/Kelesh_Bey,_Prince_of_Abkhazia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelesh Bey, Prince of Abkhazia">Keilash Bey</a> in 1803, shortly after the incorporation of eastern Georgia into the expanding Tsarist empire (1801). However, the pro-<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Turkey">Ottoman</a> orientation prevailed for a short time after his assassination by his son <a href="/wiki/Aslan-Bey_Shervashidze" title="Aslan-Bey Shervashidze">Aslan-Bey</a> on 2 May 1808.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On 2 July 1810, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Marines" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Marines">Russian Marines</a> <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1806%E2%80%931812)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1806\xe2\x80\x931812)">stormed Sukhum-Kale</a> and had Aslan-Bey replaced with his rival brother, <a href="/wiki/Sefer_Ali-Bey_Shervashidze" title="Sefer Ali-Bey Shervashidze">Sefer-Bey</a> (1810\xe2\x80\x931821), who had converted to Christianity and assumed the name of <a href="/wiki/George_(given_name)" title="George (given name)">George</a>. Abkhazia joined the Russian Empire as an autonomous principality, in 1810.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> However, George\'s rule, as well as that of his successors, was limited to the neighbourhood of Sukhum-Kale and the Bzyb area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War,_1828-1829" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War, 1828-1829">next Russo-Turkish war</a> strongly enhanced the Russian positions, leading to a further split in the Abkhaz elite, mainly along religious divisions. During the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> (1853\xe2\x80\x931856), Russian forces had to evacuate Abkhazia and Prince <a href="/wiki/Mikheil,_Prince_of_Abkhazia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mikheil, Prince of Abkhazia">Michael</a> (1822\xe2\x80\x931864) seemingly switched to the Ottomans.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Later on, the Russian presence strengthened and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Circassian_War" title="Russo-Circassian War">highlanders of Western Caucasia were finally subjugated</a> by Russia in 1864.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The autonomy of Abkhazia, which had functioned as a pro-Russian "buffer zone" in this troublesome region, was no longer needed by the Tsarist government and the rule of the Shervashidze came to an end; in November 1864, Prince Michael was forced to renounce his rights and resettle in <a href="/wiki/Voronezh" title="Voronezh">Voronezh</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Later that same year, Abkhazia was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> as a special military province<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> of Sukhum-Kale which was transformed, in 1883, into an <i><a href="/wiki/Okrug" title="Okrug">okrug</a></i> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Kutaisi" title="Kutaisi">Kutais</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Guberniya" class="mw-redirect" title="Guberniya">Guberniya</a></i>. Large numbers of Muslim Abkhazians, said to have constituted as much as 40% of the Abkhazian population, emigrated to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> between 1864 and 1878 with other Muslim population of Caucasus, a process known as <i><a href="/wiki/Muhajir_(Caucasus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Muhajir (Caucasus)">Muhajirism</a></i>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhaz_and_Georgian_generals_(A).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Abkhaz_and_Georgian_generals_%28A%29.jpg/220px-Abkhaz_and_Georgian_generals_%28A%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/Abkhaz_and_Georgian_generals_%28A%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="299" data-file-height="198" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhaz_and_Georgian_generals_(A).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Abkhaz and Georgian generals in the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army" title="Imperial Russian Army">Imperial Russian Army</a>, 19th century</div></div></div>\n<p>Large areas of the region were left uninhabited and many <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, Georgians, Russians and others subsequently migrated to Abkhazia, resettling much of the vacated territory.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Some Georgian historians assert that Georgian tribes (<a href="/wiki/Svans" title="Svans">Svans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mingrelians" title="Mingrelians">Mingrelians</a>) had populated Abkhazia since the time of the Colchis kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-Lortkipanidze_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lortkipanidze-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By official decision of the Russian authorities the residents of Abkhazia and Samurzakano had to study and pray in Russian. After the mass deportation of 1878, Abkhazians were left in the minority, officially branded "guilty people", and had no leader capable of mounting serious opposition to Russification.<sup id="cite_ref-Tsarism_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tsarism-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 17 March 1898 the synodal department of the Russian Orthodox Church of Georgia-Imereti, by order 2771, again prohibited teaching and the conduct of religious services in church schools and churches of the Sukhumi district in Georgian.  Mass protests by the Georgian population of Abkhazia and Samurzakano followed, news of which reached the Russian emperor. On 3 September 1898 the Holy Synod issued order 4880 which decreed that those parishes where the congregation was Mingrelians i.e. Georgians, conduct both church services and church education in Georgian, while Abkhazian parishes use <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">old Slavic</a>. In the Sukhumi district, this order was carried out in only three of 42 parishes.<sup id="cite_ref-Tsarism_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tsarism-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>  Tedo Sakhokia demanded the Russian authorities introduce Abkhazian and Georgian languages in church services and education. The official response was a criminal case brought against Tedo Sakhokia and leaders of his "Georgian Party" active in Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-Tsarism_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tsarism-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Within_the_Soviet_Union">Within the Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Within the Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg/220px-Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg.png" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg/330px-Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg/440px-Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="747" data-file-height="629" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_Caucasus_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> Caucasus (1957\xe2\x80\x9391) showing the <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Abkhaz Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Abkhaz ASSR</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian SSR</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1917" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revolution of 1917">Russian Revolution of 1917</a> led to the creation of an <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Democratic Republic of Georgia">independent Georgia</a> which included Abkhazia, in 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> German support enabled the Georgians to repel the Bolshevik threat from Abkhazia in 1918. The 1921 constitution granted Abkhazia autonomy.\n</p><p>In 1921, the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> Red Army invaded Georgia and ended its short-lived independence. Abkhazia was made a Socialist Soviet Republic (<a href="/wiki/SSR_Abkhazia" class="mw-redirect" title="SSR Abkhazia">SSR Abkhazia</a>) with the ambiguous status of a <i>treaty republic</i> associated with the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian SSR">Georgian SSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-constitution_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 1931, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> made it an autonomous republic (<a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Abkhaz Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Abkhaz Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> or in short Abkhaz ASSR) within the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian SSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Despite its nominal autonomy, it was subjected to strong direct rule from central Soviet authorities.  Under the rule of Stalin and <a href="/wiki/Lavrenti_Beria" class="mw-redirect" title="Lavrenti Beria">Beria</a> Abkhaz schools were closed, requiring Abkhaz children to study in the Georgian language.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jrl_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jrl-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The publishing of materials in Abkhazian dwindled and was eventually stopped altogether; Abkhazian schools were closed in 1945/46.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">terror of 1937-38</a>, the ruling elite was purged of Abkhaz and by 1952 over 80% of the 228 top party and government officials and enterprise managers were ethnic Georgians; there remained 34 Abkhaz, 7 Russians and 3 Armenians in these positions.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Georgia_(Soviet_Union)" title="Communist Party of Georgia (Soviet Union)">Georgian Communist Party</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Candide_Charkviani" class="mw-redirect" title="Candide Charkviani">Candide Charkviani</a> supported the Georgianization of Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The policy of repression was eased after Stalin\'s death<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and Beria\'s execution, and the Abkhaz were given a greater role in the governance of the republic.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> As in most of the smaller autonomous republics, the Soviet government encouraged the development of culture and particularly of literature.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Abkhazian ASSR was the only autonomous republic in the USSR in which the language of the titular nation (in that case Abkhazian) was confirmed in its constitution as one of its official languages.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Soviet_Georgia">Post-Soviet Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-Soviet Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Georgian%E2%80%93Abkhaz_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhaz conflict">Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhaz conflict</a></div>\n<p>As the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> began to disintegrate at the end of the 1980s, ethnic tensions grew between the Abkhaz and Georgians over Georgia\'s moves towards independence. Many Abkhaz opposed this, fearing that an independent Georgia would lead to the elimination of their autonomy, and argued instead for the establishment of Abkhazia as a separate Soviet republic in its own right. In June 1988, a manifesto defending Abkhaz distinctiveness (known as the <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_Letter" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz Letter">Abkhaz Letter</a>) was sent to Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>.\n</p><p>The Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhaz <a href="/wiki/1989_Sukhumi_riots" title="1989 Sukhumi riots">dispute turned violent</a> on 16 July 1989 in Sukhumi. Sixteen Georgians are said to have been killed and another 137 injured when they tried to enroll in a Georgian university instead of an Abkhaz one. After several days of violence, Soviet troops restored order in the city and blamed rival nationalist paramilitaries for provoking confrontations.\n</p><p>In March 1990, Georgia declared sovereignty, unilaterally nullifying treaties concluded by the Soviet government since 1921 and thereby moving closer to independence. The Republic of Georgia boycotted the 17 March 1991 <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_referendum,_1991" title="Soviet Union referendum, 1991">all-Union referendum</a> on the renewal of the Soviet Union called by Gorbachev; however, 52.3% of Abkhazia\'s population (almost all of the ethnic non-Georgian population) took part in the referendum and voted by an overwhelming majority (98.6%) to preserve the Union.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Most ethnic non-Georgians in Abkhazia later boycotted a 31 March <a href="/wiki/Georgian_independence_referendum,_1991" title="Georgian independence referendum, 1991">referendum on Georgia\'s independence</a>, which was supported by a huge majority of Georgia\'s population. Within weeks, Georgia declared independence on 9 April 1991, under former Soviet dissident <a href="/wiki/Zviad_Gamsakhurdia" title="Zviad Gamsakhurdia">Zviad Gamsakhurdia</a>. Under Gamsakhurdia, the situation was relatively calm in Abkhazia and a power-sharing agreement was soon reached between the Abkhaz and Georgian factions, granting to the Abkhaz a certain over-representation in the local legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gamsakhurdia\'s rule was soon challenged by armed opposition groups, under the command of <a href="/wiki/Tengiz_Kitovani" title="Tengiz Kitovani">Tengiz Kitovani</a>, that forced him to flee the country in a military coup in January 1992. Former Soviet foreign minister and architect of the disintegration of the USSR <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Shevardnadze" title="Eduard Shevardnadze">Eduard Shevardnadze</a> became the country\'s head of state, inheriting a government dominated by hard-line Georgian nationalists. He was not an ethnic nationalist but did little to avoid being seen as supporting his administration\'s dominant figures and the leaders of the coup that swept him to power.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On 21 February 1992, Georgia\'s ruling Military Council announced that it was abolishing the Soviet-era constitution and restoring the 1921 Constitution of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Democratic Republic of Georgia">Democratic Republic of Georgia</a>. Many Abkhaz interpreted this as an abolition of their autonomous status, although the 1921 constitution contained a provision for the region\'s autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On 23 July 1992, the Abkhaz faction in the republic\'s Supreme Council declared effective independence from Georgia, although the session was boycotted by ethnic Georgian deputies and the gesture went unrecognised by any other country. The Abkhaz leadership launched a campaign of ousting Georgian officials from their offices, a process which was accompanied by violence. In the meantime, the Abkhaz leader <a href="/wiki/Vladislav_Ardzinba" title="Vladislav Ardzinba">Vladislav Ardzinba</a> intensified his ties with hard-line Russian politicians and military elite and declared he was ready for a war with Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-Svante_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Svante-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abkhazian_War">Abkhazian War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Abkhazian War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992%E2%80%9393)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Abkhazia (1992\xe2\x80\x9393)">War in Abkhazia (1992\xe2\x80\x9393)</a></div>\n<p>In August 1992, the Georgian government accused Gamsakhurdia\'s supporters of kidnapping Georgia\'s Interior Minister and holding him captive in Abkhazia. The Georgian government dispatched 3,000 soldiers to the region, ostensibly to restore order. The Abkhaz were relatively unarmed at this time and the Georgian troops were able to march into Sukhumi with relatively little resistance<sup id="cite_ref-mirsky1_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirsky1-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and subsequently engaged in ethnically based pillage, looting, assault, and murder.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The Abkhaz units were forced to retreat to <a href="/wiki/Gudauta" title="Gudauta">Gudauta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tkvarcheli" title="Tkvarcheli">Tkvarcheli</a>.\n</p><p>The Abkhaz military defeat was met with a hostile response by the self-styled <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_Mountain_Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Confederation of Mountain Peoples of the Caucasus">Confederation of Mountain Peoples of the Caucasus</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Umbrella_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Umbrella group">umbrella group</a> uniting a number of movements in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>, including elements of <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abaza_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abaza people">Abazins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chechen_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Chechen people">Chechens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a> and hundreds of volunteer paramilitaries and mercenaries from Russia, including the then-little-known <a href="/wiki/Shamil_Basayev" title="Shamil Basayev">Shamil Basayev</a>, later a leader of the anti-Moscow Chechen secessionists.  They sided with the Abkhaz separatists to fight against the Georgian government. In the case of Basayev, it has been suggested that when he and the members of his battalion came to Abkhazia, they received training by the Russian Army (though others dispute this), presenting another possible motive.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In September, the Abkhaz and Russian paramilitaries mounted a major <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gagra" title="Battle of Gagra">offensive against Gagra</a> after breaking a cease-fire, which drove the Georgian forces out of large swathes of the republic. Shevardnadze\'s government accused Russia of giving covert military support to the rebels with the aim of "detaching from Georgia its native territory and the Georgia-Russian frontier land". 1992 ended with the rebels in control of much of Abkhazia northwest of Sukhumi.\n</p><p>The conflict was in stalemate until July 1993, when Abkhaz separatist militias launched an abortive attack on Georgian-held Sukhumi. They surrounded and heavily shelled the capital, where Shevardnadze was trapped. The warring sides <a href="/wiki/Sochi_agreement" title="Sochi agreement">agreed to a Russian-brokered truce in Sochi</a> at the end of July. But the ceasefire broke down again on 16 September 1993. Abkhaz forces, with armed support from outside Abkhazia, launched attacks on Sukhumi and Ochamchira. Notwithstanding UN Security Council\'s call for the immediate cessation of hostilities and its condemnation of the violation of the ceasefire by the Abkhaz side, fighting continued.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> After ten days of heavy fighting, Sukhumi was taken by Abkhazian forces on 27 September 1993. Shevardnadze narrowly escaped death, after vowing to stay in the city no matter what. He was forced to flee when separatist <a href="/wiki/Sniper" title="Sniper">snipers</a> fired on the hotel where he was staying. Abkhaz, North Caucasian militants, and their allies committed numerous atrocities<sup id="cite_ref-hrwreport_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrwreport-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> against the city\'s remaining ethnic Georgians, in what has been dubbed the <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Sukhumi Massacre">Sukhumi Massacre</a>. The mass killings and destruction continued for two weeks, leaving thousands dead and missing.\n</p><p>The Abkhaz forces quickly overran the rest of Abkhazia as the Georgian government faced a second threat: an uprising by the supporters of the deposed Zviad Gamsakhurdia in the region of Mingrelia (Samegrelo). Only a small region of eastern Abkhazia, the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Abkhazia" title="Upper Abkhazia">upper Kodori gorge</a>, remained under Georgian control (until 2008).\n</p><p>During the war, gross human rights violations were reported on both sides (see <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> report).<sup id="cite_ref-hrwreport_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrwreport-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Georgian troops have been accused of having committed looting<sup id="cite_ref-mirsky1_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirsky1-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and murders "for the purpose of terrorising, robbing and driving the Abkhaz population out of their homes"<sup id="cite_ref-hrwreport_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrwreport-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> in the first phase of the war (according to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>), while Georgia blames the Abkhaz forces and their allies for the ethnic cleansing of Georgians in Abkhazia, which has also been recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE) Summits in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> (1994),<sup id="cite_ref-osce1_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osce1-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> (1996)<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> (1999).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_cleansing_of_Georgians">Ethnic cleansing of Georgians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ethnic cleansing of Georgians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Georgians_in_Abkhazia" title="Ethnic cleansing of Georgians in Abkhazia">Ethnic cleansing of Georgians in Abkhazia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg/220px-Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg/330px-Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg/440px-Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="884" data-file-height="599" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhazia_genocide_anniversary_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2005 commemoration of the ethnic cleansing in Abkhazia, held on its 12th anniversary in Tbilisi.</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992-1993)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Abkhazia (1992-1993)">1992 War</a>, Georgians made up nearly half of Abkhazia\'s population, while less than one-fifth of the population was <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz people">Abkhaz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As the war progressed, confronted with hundreds of thousands of ethnic Georgians who were unwilling to leave their homes, the Abkhaz separatists implemented the process of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> in order to expel and eliminate the Georgian ethnic population in Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The exact number of those killed during the ethnic cleansing is disputed, however, it ranges from 8,000 to 10,000 people, not including the civilians who were killed in <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1998)" title="War in Abkhazia (1998)">1998</a> during the separatist onslaught on <a href="/wiki/Gali_District,_Abkhazia" title="Gali District, Abkhazia">Gali</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Roughly up to 250,000 ethnic Georgians were expelled from their homes. Slightly over 200,000 Georgians remain displaced in Georgia proper.<sup id="cite_ref-Abkhazia_Today_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abkhazia_Today-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The campaign of ethnic cleansing also included Russians, Armenians, Greeks, moderate Abkhaz and other minor ethnic groups living in Abkhazia. More than 20,000 houses owned by ethnic Georgians were destroyed. Hundreds of schools, kindergartens, churches, hospitals, historical monuments were pillaged and destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Following the process of ethnic cleansing and mass expulsion, the population of Abkhazia has been reduced to 216,000, from 525,000 in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of about 250,000 Georgian refugees, some 60,000 Georgian refugees subsequently returned to Abkhazia\'s <a href="/wiki/Gali_District,_Abkhazia" title="Gali District, Abkhazia">Gali District</a> between 1994 and 1998, but tens of thousands were displaced again when fighting resumed in the Gali District in 1998. Nevertheless, between 40,000 and 60,000 refugees have returned to the Gali District since 1998, including persons commuting daily across the ceasefire line and those migrating seasonally in accordance with agricultural cycles.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The human rights situation remained precarious for a while in the Georgian-populated areas of the Gali District. The United Nations and other international organisations have been fruitlessly urging the Abkhaz <i>de facto</i> authorities "to refrain from adopting measures incompatible with the right to return and with international human rights standards, such as discriminatory legislation... [and] to cooperate in the establishment of a permanent international human rights office in Gali and to admit United Nations civilian police without further delay."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Key officials of the Gali District are virtually all ethnic Abkhaz, though their support staff are ethnic Georgian.<sup id="cite_ref-Today_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Today-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war">Post-war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Post-war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Georgian%E2%80%93Abkhaz_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhaz conflict">Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhaz conflict</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg/220px-Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg/330px-Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg/440px-Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Apsua_Holding_Apsny_Flag.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Abkhazians carrying the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Abkhazia" title="Flag of Abkhazia">republic\'s flags</a> in a parade.</div></div></div>\n<p>Presidential elections were held in Abkhazia on 3 October 2004. Russia supported <a href="/wiki/Raul_Khadjimba" class="mw-redirect" title="Raul Khadjimba">Raul Khadjimba</a>, the prime minister backed by the ailing outgoing separatist President <a href="/wiki/Vladislav_Ardzinba" title="Vladislav Ardzinba">Vladislav Ardzinba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Posters of Russia\'s President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> together with Khadjimba, who, like Putin, had worked as a <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a> official, were everywhere in Sukhumi.<sup id="cite_ref-kkuzel62425_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kkuzel62425-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Deputies of Russia\'s parliament and Russian singers, led by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kobzon" title="Joseph Kobzon">Joseph Cobsohn</a>, a State Duma deputy and a popular singer, came to Abkhazia, campaigning for Khadjimba.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However <a href="/wiki/Raul_Khadjimba" class="mw-redirect" title="Raul Khadjimba">Raul Khadjimba</a> lost the elections to <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bagapsh" title="Sergei Bagapsh">Sergei Bagapsh</a>. The tense situation in the republic led to the cancellation of the election results by the Supreme Court. After that, a deal was struck between former rivals to run jointly, with Bagapsh as a presidential candidate and Khadjimba as a vice presidential candidate. They received more than 90% of the votes in the new election.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2006, Georgian forces launched a successful police operation against the rebelled administrator of the Georgian-populated <a href="/wiki/Kodori_Gorge" class="mw-redirect" title="Kodori Gorge">Kodori Gorge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emzar_Kvitsiani" title="Emzar Kvitsiani">Emzar Kvitsiani</a>. Kvitsiani had been appointed by the previous president of Georgia <a href="/wiki/Edvard_Shevardnadze" class="mw-redirect" title="Edvard Shevardnadze">Edvard Shevardnadze</a> and refused to recognise the authority of president <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a>, who succeeded Shevardnadze after the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Revolution" title="Rose Revolution">Rose Revolution</a>. Although Kvitsiani escaped capture by Georgian police, the Kodori Gorge was brought back under the control of the central government in <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Sporadic acts of violence continued throughout the postwar years. Despite the peacekeeping status of the Russian peacekeepers in Abkhazia, Georgian officials routinely claimed that Russian peacekeepers were inciting violence by supplying Abkhaz rebels with arms and financial support. Russian support of Abkhazia became pronounced when the <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> became the <a href="/wiki/De_facto_currency" title="De facto currency">de facto currency</a> and Russia began issuing passports to the population of Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Georgia has also accused Russia of violating its airspace by sending helicopters to <a href="/wiki/2007_Georgia_helicopter_attack_incident" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Georgia helicopter attack incident">attack Georgian-controlled towns in the Kodori Gorge</a>. In April 2008, a Russian MiG \xe2\x80\x93 prohibited from Georgian airspace, including Abkhazia \xe2\x80\x93 shot down a Georgian <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">UAV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 August 2008, Abkhazian forces fired on Georgian forces in <a href="/wiki/Kodori_Gorge" class="mw-redirect" title="Kodori Gorge">Kodori Gorge</a>. This coincided with the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia war">2008 South Ossetia war</a> where Russia decided to support the Ossetian separatists who had been attacked by Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The conflict escalated into a full-scale war between the Russian Federation and the Republic of Georgia. On 10 August 2008, an estimated 9,000 Russian soldiers entered Abkhazia ostensibly to reinforce the Russian peacekeepers in the republic. About 1,000 Abkhazian soldiers moved to expel the residual Georgian forces within Abkhazia in the Upper Kodori Gorge.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> By 12 August the Georgian forces and civilians had evacuated the last part of Abkhazia under Georgian government control. Russia recognised the <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">independence of Abkhazia</a> on 26 August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> This was followed by the annulment of the 1994 ceasefire agreement and the termination of <a href="/wiki/UNOMIG" class="mw-redirect" title="UNOMIG">UN</a> and <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a> monitoring missions.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On 28 August 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Georgia" title="Parliament of Georgia">Parliament of Georgia</a> passed a resolution declaring Abkhazia a Russian-occupied territory.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since independence was recognised by Russia, a series of controversial agreements were made between the Abkhazian government and the Russian Federation that leased or sold a number of key state assets and relinquished control over the borders. In May 2009 several opposition parties and war veteran groups protested against these deals complaining that they undermined state sovereignty and risked exchanging one colonial power (Georgia) for another (Russia).<sup id="cite_ref-rfe_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfe-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The Vice President, <a href="/wiki/Raul_Khadjimba" class="mw-redirect" title="Raul Khadjimba">Raul Khadjimba</a>, resigned on 28 May saying he agreed with the criticism the opposition had made.<sup id="cite_ref-apress0528_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apress0528-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, a conference of opposition parties nominated Raul Khadjimba as their candidate in the December 2009 <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_presidential_election,_2009" title="Abkhazian presidential election, 2009">Abkhazian presidential election</a> won by <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bagapsh" title="Sergei Bagapsh">Sergei Bagapsh</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_unrest_in_2014">Political unrest in 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Political unrest in 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_Revolution" title="Abkhazian Revolution">Abkhazian Revolution</a></div>\n<p>In the spring of 2014, the opposition submitted an ultimatum to President <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Ankvab" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksandr Ankvab">Aleksandr Ankvab</a> to dismiss the government and make radical reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-khadzhimba_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khadzhimba-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> On 27 May 2014, in the centre of <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">Sukhumi</a>, 10,000 supporters of the Abkhaz opposition gathered for a mass demonstration.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On the same day, Ankvab\'s headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">Sukhumi</a> was stormed by opposition groups led by <a href="/wiki/Raul_Khadjimba" class="mw-redirect" title="Raul Khadjimba">Raul Khadjimba</a>, forcing him into flight to <a href="/wiki/Gudauta" title="Gudauta">Gudauta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The opposition claimed that the protests were sparked by poverty, but the main point of contention was President Ankvab\'s liberal policy towards ethnic Georgians in the <a href="/wiki/Gali_District,_Abkhazia" title="Gali District, Abkhazia">Gali region</a>. The opposition said these policies could endanger Abkhazia\'s ethnic Abkhazian identity.<sup id="cite_ref-khadzhimba_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khadzhimba-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Ankvab fled the capital, on 31 May, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Assembly_of_Abkhazia" title="People&#39;s Assembly of Abkhazia">People\'s Assembly of Abkhazia</a> appointed parliamentary speaker <a href="/wiki/Valery_Bganba" class="mw-redirect" title="Valery Bganba">Valery Bganba</a> as acting president, declaring Ankvab unable to serve. It also decided to hold an early presidential election on 24 August 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Ankvab soon declared his formal resignation, although he accused his opponents of acting immorally and violating the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Khajimba was later <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_presidential_election,_2014" title="Abkhazian presidential election, 2014">elected president</a>, taking office in September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2014, Vladimir Putin moved to formalise the Abkhazian military\'s relationship as part of the Russian armed forces, signing a treaty with Khajimba.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The Georgian government denounced the agreement as "a step towards annexation".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Georgia_high_detail_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Georgia_high_detail_map.png/220px-Georgia_high_detail_map.png" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Georgia_high_detail_map.png/330px-Georgia_high_detail_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Georgia_high_detail_map.png/440px-Georgia_high_detail_map.png 2x" data-file-width="2529" data-file-height="1872" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Georgia_high_detail_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Georgia highlighting Abkhazia (green) and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a> (purple).</div></div></div>\n<p>Abkhazia, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Artsakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a> are post-Soviet "<a href="/wiki/Frozen_conflict" title="Frozen conflict">frozen conflict</a>" zones.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> These four states maintain friendly relations with each other and form the <a href="/wiki/Community_for_Democracy_and_Rights_of_Nations" title="Community for Democracy and Rights of Nations">Community for Democracy and Rights of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-recognition1_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recognition1-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Russia and Nicaragua officially recognised Abkhazia after the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War" title="Russo-Georgian War">Russo-Georgian War</a>. Venezuela recognised Abkhazia in September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In December 2009, Nauru recognised Abkhazia, reportedly in return for $50 million in humanitarian aid from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The unrecognised republic of Transnistria and the partially recognised republic of South Ossetia have recognised Abkhazia since 2006. Abkhazia is also a member of the  <a href="/wiki/Unrepresented_Nations_and_Peoples_Organization" title="Unrepresented Nations and Peoples Organization">Unrepresented Nations and Peoples Organization</a> (UNPO).\n</p><p>A majority of sovereign states recognise Abkhazia as an integral part of Georgia and support its <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> according to the principles of <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>, although Belarus has expressed sympathy toward the recognition of Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Some have officially noted Abkhazia as under <a href="/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia" title="Occupied territories of Georgia">occupation by the Russian military</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The United Nations has been urging both sides to settle the dispute through diplomatic dialogue and ratifying the final status of Abkhazia in the Georgian constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-hrwreport_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrwreport-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> However, the Abkhaz <i>de facto</i> government considers Abkhazia a sovereign country even if it is recognised by few other countries. In early 2000, then-UN Special Representative of the Secretary General Dieter Boden and the Group of Friends of Georgia, consisting of the representatives of Russia, the United States, Britain, France, and Germany, drafted and informally presented a document to the parties outlining a possible distribution of competencies between the Abkhaz and Georgian authorities, based on core respect for Georgian territorial integrity. The Abkhaz side, however, has never accepted the paper as a basis for negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Eventually, Russia also withdrew its approval of the document.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> In 2005 and 2008, the Georgian government offered Abkhazia a high degree of <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a> and possible <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal structure</a> within the borders and <a href="/wiki/Jurisdiction" title="Jurisdiction">jurisdiction</a> of Georgia.\n</p><p>On 18 October 2006, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Assembly_of_Abkhazia" title="People&#39;s Assembly of Abkhazia">People\'s Assembly of Abkhazia</a> passed a resolution, calling upon Russia, international organisations and the rest of the international community to recognise Abkhaz independence on the basis that Abkhazia possesses all the properties of an independent state.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The United Nations has reaffirmed "the commitment of all Member States to the sovereignty, independence and territorial integrity of Georgia within its internationally recognised borders" and outlined the basic principles of conflict resolution which call for immediate return of all displaced persons and for non-resumption of hostilities.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Georgia accuses the Abkhaz secessionists of having conducted a deliberate campaign of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnic cleansing</a> of up to 250,000 Georgians, a claim supported by the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE; Budapest, Lisbon and Istanbul declaration).<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The UN Security Council has avoided the use of the term "ethnic cleansing" but has affirmed "the unacceptability of the demographic changes resulting from the conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> On 15 May 2008, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> adopted a non-binding resolution recognising the right of all refugees (including victims of reported "ethnic cleansing") to return to Abkhazia and to retain or regain their property rights there. It "regretted" the attempts to alter pre-war demographic composition and called for the "rapid development of a timetable to ensure the prompt voluntary return of all refugees and internally displaced persons to their homes."<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 March 2008, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Georgia" title="President of Georgia">President of Georgia</a> <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a> unveiled his government\'s new proposals to Abkhazia: the broadest possible
