autonomy within the framework of a Georgian state, a joint free economic zone, representation in the central authorities including the post of vice-president with the right to veto Abkhaz-related decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The Abkhaz leader <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bagapsh" title="Sergei Bagapsh">Sergei Bagapsh</a> rejected these new initiatives as "propaganda", leading to Georgia\'s complaints that this scepticism was "triggered by Russia, rather than by real mood of the Abkhaz people."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg/220px-Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg/330px-Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg/440px-Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1093" data-file-height="787" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Russia_in_Sukhumi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Russian embassy in Sukhumi</div></div></div>\n<p>On 3 July 2008, the <a href="/wiki/OSCE_Parliamentary_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE Parliamentary Assembly">OSCE Parliamentary Assembly</a> passed a resolution at its annual session in <a href="/wiki/Astana" title="Astana">Astana</a>, expressing concern over Russia\xe2\x80\x99s recent moves in breakaway Abkhazia. The resolution calls on the Russian authorities to refrain from maintaining ties with the breakaway regions "in any manner that would constitute a challenge to the sovereignty of Georgia" and also urges Russia "to abide by OSCE standards and generally accepted international norms with respect to the threat or use of force to resolve conflicts in relations with other participating States."<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 July 2012, the <a href="/wiki/OSCE_Parliamentary_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE Parliamentary Assembly">OSCE Parliamentary Assembly</a> passed a resolution at its annual session in <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, underlining Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s territorial integrity and referring to breakaway Abkhazia and South Ossetia as "occupied territories". The resolution "urges the Government and the Parliament of the Russian Federation, as well as the de facto authorities of Abkhazia, Georgia and South Ossetia, Georgia, to allow the European Union Monitoring Mission unimpeded access to the occupied territories." It also says that the OSCE Parliamentary Assembly is "concerned about the humanitarian situation of the displaced persons both in Georgia and in the occupied territories of Abkhazia, Georgia and South Ossetia, Georgia, as well as the denial of the right of return to their places of living." The Assembly is the parliamentary dimension of the OSCE with 320 lawmakers from the organisation\xe2\x80\x99s 57 participating states, including Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_on_Occupied_Territories_of_Georgia">Law on Occupied Territories of Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Law on Occupied Territories of Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia" title="Occupied territories of Georgia">Occupied territories of Georgia</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(August 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_(2011-2016_Data).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_%282011-2016_Data%29.svg/220px-Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_%282011-2016_Data%29.svg.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_%282011-2016_Data%29.svg/330px-Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_%282011-2016_Data%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_%282011-2016_Data%29.svg/440px-Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_%282011-2016_Data%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="980" data-file-height="735" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Military_Bases_in_Abkhazia_(2011-2016_Data).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian military bases in Abkhazia as of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In late October 2008 President Saakashvili signed into law legislation on the occupied territories passed by the Georgian Parliament. The law covers the breakaway regions of Abkhazia and Tskhinvali (territories of former South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The law spells out restrictions on free movement and economic activity in the territories. In particular, according to the law, foreign citizens should enter the two breakaway regions only through Georgia proper. Entry into Abkhazia should be carried out from the <a href="/wiki/Zugdidi_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Zugdidi District">Zugdidi District</a> and into South Ossetia from the <a href="/wiki/Gori_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Gori District">Gori District</a>. The major road leading to South Ossetia from the rest of Georgia passes through the Gori District.\n</p><p>The legislation, however, also lists "special" cases in which entry into the breakaway regions will not be regarded as illegal. It stipulates that a special permit on entry into the breakaway regions can be issued if the trip there "serves Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s state interests; peaceful resolution of the conflict; de-occupation or humanitarian purposes." The law also bans any type of economic activity \xe2\x80\x93 entrepreneurial or non-entrepreneurial, if such activities require permits, licenses or registration in accordance with Georgian legislation. It also bans air, sea and railway communications and international transit via the regions, mineral exploration and money transfers. The provision covering economic activities is retroactive, going back to 1990.\n</p><p>The law says that the Russian Federation \xe2\x80\x93 the state which has carried out military occupation \xe2\x80\x93 is fully responsible for the violation of human rights in Abkhazia and South Ossetia. The Russian Federation, according to the document, is also responsible for compensation of material and moral damage inflicted on Georgian citizens, stateless persons and foreign citizens, who are in Georgia and enter the occupied territories with appropriate permits. The law also says that de facto state agencies and officials operating in the occupied territories are regarded by Georgia as illegal. The law will remain in force until "the full restoration of Georgian jurisdiction" over the breakaway regions is realised.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Status-neutral_passports">Status-neutral passports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Status-neutral passports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_passport" title="Abkhazian passport">Abkhazian passport</a></div>\n<p>Currently Georgia considers all residents of Abkhazia its citizens, while they see themselves as Abkhaz citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-Abkhazia_Today_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abkhazia_Today-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the summer of 2011 the Parliament of Georgia adopted a package of legislative amendments providing for the issuance of neutral identification and travel documents to residents of Abkhazia and the former South Ossetian autonomous province of Georgia. The document allows travelling abroad as well as enjoying social benefits existing in Georgia. The new neutral identification and travel documents were called "neutral passports".<sup id="cite_ref-Neutral_Passports_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neutral_Passports-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to Georgian officials, the "neutral passports" lacked any symbols of Georgia and only bore a registration number and an individual number. Moscow argued it was Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s "cunning ploy" because the passports contained Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s code and the Georgian Interior Ministry as the issuing body.\n</p><p>Abkhazia\xe2\x80\x99s Foreign Ministry expressed concerns about some countries recognising the "neutral passports." The ministry also said an increasing number of Abkhazian residents with Russian passports were being denied <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen visas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of May 2013, neutral documents have been recognised by Japan, the Czech Republic, Latvia, Lithuania, Slovakia, the United States, Bulgaria, Poland, Israel, Estonia and Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-Neutral_Passports_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neutral_Passports-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to Russian media, the President of Republic of Abkhazia, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Ankvab" title="Alexander Ankvab">Alexander Ankvab</a> threatened international organisations that accepted neutral passports, saying during a meeting with the leadership of the foreign ministry that "international organizations that suggest the so-called neutral passports, will leave Abkhazia."<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_involvement">Russian involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Russian involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_17_September_2008-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The leaders of Abkhazia, Russia and South Ossetia, shortly after the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia War">2008 war</a>. Left to right: South Ossetian President <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Kokoity" title="Eduard Kokoity">Eduard Kokoity</a>; <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Russia)">Russian Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Lavrov" title="Sergey Lavrov">Sergey Lavrov</a>; Abkhazian President <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bagapsh" title="Sergei Bagapsh">Sergei Bagapsh</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Georgian%E2%80%93Abkhaz_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhaz conflict">Georgian\xe2\x80\x93Abkhaz conflict</a>, the Russian authorities and <a href="/wiki/Russian_military" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian military">military</a> supplied logistical and military aid to the separatist side.<sup id="cite_ref-hrwreport_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrwreport-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Today, Russia still maintains a strong political and military influence over separatist rule in Abkhazia. Russia has also issued passports to the citizens of Abkhazia since 2000 (as Abkhazian passports cannot be used for international travel) and subsequently paid them retirement pensions and other monetary benefits. More than 80% of the Abkhazian population had received Russian passports by 2006. As Russian citizens living abroad, Abkhazians do not pay Russian taxes or serve in the Russian Army.<sup id="cite_ref-crisisgroup_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crisisgroup-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> About 53,000 Abkhazian passports have been issued as of May 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Moscow, at certain times, hinted that it might recognise Abkhazia and South Ossetia when Western countries recognised the independence of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, suggesting that they had created a <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_independence_precedent" title="Kosovo independence precedent">precedent</a>. Following Kosovo\'s declaration of independence, the Russian parliament released a joint statement reading: "Now that the situation in Kosovo has become an international precedent, Russia should take into account the Kosovo scenario... when considering ongoing territorial conflicts."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Initially Russia continued to delay recognition of both of these republics. However, on 16 April 2008, the outgoing Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> instructed his government to establish official ties with South Ossetia and Abkhazia, leading to Georgia\'s condemnation of what it described as an attempt at "de facto annexation"<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> and criticism from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, and several Western governments.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Later in April 2008, Russia accused Georgia of trying to exploit NATO support in order to control Abkhazia by force and announced it would increase its military presence in the region, pledging to retaliate militarily against Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s efforts. The Georgian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Lado_Gurgenidze" title="Lado Gurgenidze">Lado Gurgenidze</a> said Georgia will treat any additional troops in Abkhazia as "aggressors".<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In response to the Georgian <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia War">invasion of South Ossetia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Assembly of Russia">Federal Assembly of Russia</a> called an extraordinary session for 25 August 2008 to discuss recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Following a unanimous resolution that was passed by both houses of the parliament calling on the Russian president to recognise independence of the breakaway republics,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Russian president, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a>, officially recognised both on 26 August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Russian recognition<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> was condemned by <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> nations, OSCE and <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> nations<sup id="cite_ref-civil.ge_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civil.ge-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> due to "violation of <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> and international law".<sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> stated that sovereign states have to decide themselves whether they want to recognise the independence of disputed regions.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Russia has started work on the establishment of a naval base in Ochamchire by dredging the coast to allow the passage of their larger naval vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> As a response to the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_sea_blockade_of_Abkhazia" title="Georgian sea blockade of Abkhazia">Georgian sea blockade of Abkhazia</a>, in which the Georgian coast guard had been detaining ships heading to and from Abkhazia, Russia began patrolling the Black Sea to protect Abkhazia-transiting ships and detaining  Georgian ships navigating Abkhazian waters.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The extent of Russian influence in Abkhazia has caused some locals to say Abkhazia is under full Russian control, but they still prefer Russian influence over Georgian.<sup id="cite_ref-Perils_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perils-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SpyRepublic_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpyRepublic-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PanIntoFire_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PanIntoFire-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-InterestsDiverge_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InterestsDiverge-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_involvement">International involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1702" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE-%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B7%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Border checkpoint on the <a href="/wiki/Psou_River" title="Psou River">Psou River</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The UN has played various roles during the conflict and peace process: a military role through its observer mission (<a href="/wiki/UNOMIG" class="mw-redirect" title="UNOMIG">UNOMIG</a>); dual diplomatic roles through the Security Council and the appointment of a Special Envoy, succeeded by a Special Representative to the Secretary-General; a humanitarian role (<a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a> and <a href="/wiki/UNOCHA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNOCHA">UNOCHA</a>); a development role (<a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>); a human rights role (<a href="/wiki/UNHCHR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCHR">UNHCHR</a>); and a low-key capacity and confidence-building role (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Volunteers" title="United Nations Volunteers">UNV</a>). The UN\xe2\x80\x99s position has been that there will be no forcible change in international borders. Any settlement must be freely negotiated and based on autonomy for Abkhazia legitimised by referendum under international observation once the multiethnic population has returned.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> According to Western interpretations the intervention did not contravene international law since Georgia, as a sovereign state, had the right to secure order on its territory and protect its territorial integrity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The OSCE has increasingly engaged in dialogue with officials and civil society representatives in Abkhazia, especially from <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-governmental organisation">non-governmental organisations</a> (NGO)s and the <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Abkhazia" title="Media in Abkhazia">media</a>, regarding human dimension standards in the region and is considering a presence in Gali. The OSCE expressed concern and condemnation over ethnic cleansing of Georgians in Abkhazia during the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> Summit Decision<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> and later at the Lisbon Summit Declaration in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The USA rejects the unilateral secession of Abkhazia and urges its integration into Georgia as an autonomous unit. In 1998 the USA announced its readiness to allocate up to $15 million for rehabilitation of infrastructure in the Gali region if substantial progress is made in the peace process. <a href="/wiki/USAID" class="mw-redirect" title="USAID">USAID</a> has already funded some humanitarian initiatives for Abkhazia. The USA has in recent years significantly increased its military support to the Georgian armed forces but has stated that it would not condone any moves towards peace enforcement in Abkhazia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On 22 August 2006, Senator <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lugar" title="Richard Lugar">Richard Lugar</a>, then visiting Georgia\'s capital Tbilisi, joined Georgian politicians in criticism of the Russian peacekeeping mission, stating that "the U.S. administration supports the Georgian government\xe2\x80\x99s insistence on the withdrawal of Russian peacekeepers from the conflict zones in Abkhazia and the Tskhinvali district".<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 October 2006, <a href="/wiki/Javier_Solana" title="Javier Solana">Javier Solana</a>, the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_for_the_Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="High Representative for the Common Foreign and Security Policy">High Representative for the Common Foreign and Security Policy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, ruled out the possibility of replacing the Russian peacekeepers with the EU force.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>  On 10 October 2006, EU South Caucasus envoy <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peter_Semneby&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peter Semneby (page does not exist)">Peter Semneby</a> noted that "Russia\'s actions in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Georgian-Russian_espionage_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 Georgian-Russian espionage controversy">Georgia spy row</a> have damaged its credibility as a neutral peacekeeper in the EU\'s Black Sea neighbourhood."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 October 2006, the UN Security Council unanimously adopted a resolution, based on a Group of Friends of the Secretary-General draft, extending the <a href="/wiki/UNOMIG" class="mw-redirect" title="UNOMIG">UNOMIG</a> mission until 15 April 2007. Acknowledging that the "new and tense situation" resulted, at least in part, from the Georgian special forces\' operation in the upper Kodori Valley, the resolution urged the country to ensure that no troops unauthorised by the <a href="/wiki/Agreement_on_a_Cease-fire_and_Separation_of_Forces" title="Agreement on a Cease-fire and Separation of Forces">Moscow ceasefire agreement</a> were present in that area. It urged the leadership of the Abkhaz side to address seriously the need for a dignified, secure return of refugees and internally displaced persons and to reassure the local population in the Gali district that their residency rights and identity will be respected. The Georgian side is "once again urged to address seriously legitimate Abkhaz security concerns, to avoid steps that could be seen as threatening and to refrain from militant rhetoric and provocative actions, especially in upper Kodori Valley."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Calling on both parties to follow up on dialogue initiatives, it further urged them to comply fully with all previous agreements regarding non-violence and confidence-building, in particular those concerning the separation of forces. Regarding the disputed role of the peacekeepers from the Commonwealth of Independent States (CIS), the Council stressed the importance of close, effective cooperation between UNOMIG and that force and looked to all sides to continue to extend the necessary cooperation to them. At the same time, the document reaffirmed the "commitment of all Member States to the sovereignty, independence and territorial integrity of Georgia within its internationally recognised borders."<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/HALO_Trust" title="HALO Trust">HALO Trust</a>, an international non-profit organisation that specialises in the removal of the debris of war, has been active in Abkhazia since 1999 and has completed the removal of landmines in Sukhumi and Gali districts. It declared Abkhazia "mine free" in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main NGO working in Abkhazia is the France-based international NGO <a href="/w/index.php?title=Premi%C3%A8re-Urgence&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Premi\xc3\xa8re-Urgence (page does not exist)">Premi\xc3\xa8re-Urgence</a> (PU):<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> PU has been implementing rehabilitation and economical revival programmes to support the vulnerable populations affected by the frozen conflict for almost 10 years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Russia does not allow the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Monitoring_Mission" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union Monitoring Mission">European Union Monitoring Mission</a> (EUMM) to enter Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Abkhazia" title="Foreign relations of Abkhazia">Foreign relations of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<p>Abkhazia was an unrecognised state for most of its history. The following is a list of political entities that formally recognise Abkhazia.\n</p><p><b>UN member states</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia"><img alt="Russia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> recognised Abkhazia on 26 August 2008 after the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War" title="Russo-Georgian War">Russo-Georgian War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chinadaily.com.cn_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chinadaily.com.cn-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua"><img alt="Nicaragua" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/35px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg/46px-Flag_of_Nicaragua.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> recognised Abkhazia on 5 September 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-ncrg_recognition_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncrg_recognition-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela"><img alt="Venezuela" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Venezuela.svg/23px-Flag_of_Venezuela.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Venezuela.svg/35px-Flag_of_Venezuela.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Venezuela.svg/45px-Flag_of_Venezuela.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> recognised Abkhazia on 10 September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru"><img alt="Nauru" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Flag_of_Nauru.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nauru.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Flag_of_Nauru.svg/35px-Flag_of_Nauru.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Flag_of_Nauru.svg/46px-Flag_of_Nauru.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> recognised Abkhazia on 15 December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_nauru_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes_nauru-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria"><img alt="Syria" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Flag_of_Syria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Syria.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Flag_of_Syria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Syria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Flag_of_Syria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Syria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> recognized Abkhazia on 29 May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>Partially recognised and unrecognised territories</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia"><img alt="South Ossetia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg/46px-Flag_of_South_Ossetia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" /></a></span> <a href="#cite_note-recognition1-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria"><img alt="Transnistria" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Flag_of_Transnistria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Transnistria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="700" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a> recognised Abkhazia on 17 November 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-recognition1_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recognition1-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh"><img alt="Republic of Artsakh" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_Artsakh.svg/23px-Flag_of_Artsakh.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_Artsakh.svg/35px-Flag_of_Artsakh.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Flag_of_Artsakh.svg/46px-Flag_of_Artsakh.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="540" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Republic of Artsakh</a> recognised Abkhazia on 17 November 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>Former recognition</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu"><img alt="Vanuatu" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Vanuatu.svg/23px-Flag_of_Vanuatu.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Vanuatu.svg/35px-Flag_of_Vanuatu.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Vanuatu.svg/46px-Flag_of_Vanuatu.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="360" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia%E2%80%93Vanuatu_relations" title="Abkhazia\xe2\x80\x93Vanuatu relations">recognised</a> Abkhazia on 23 May 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-vanuatu_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanuatu-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> but withdrew recognition on 20 May 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu"><img alt="Tuvalu" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg/46px-Flag_of_Tuvalu.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> recognised Abkhazia on 18 September 2011 <sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> but withdrew recognition on 31 March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_and_climate_of_Abkhazia" class="mw-redirect" title="Geography and climate of Abkhazia">Geography and climate of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Agepsta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Agepsta.jpg/220px-Agepsta.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Agepsta.jpg/330px-Agepsta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Agepsta.jpg/440px-Agepsta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2570" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Agepsta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"View of Mount Agepsta and Turyi gory (Tur Mountains) from the top of Kamennyi Stolb, Aibga Ridge.", 2014.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ritsa1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ritsa1.jpg/220px-Ritsa1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ritsa1.jpg/330px-Ritsa1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Ritsa1.jpg/440px-Ritsa1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ritsa1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Ritsa" title="Lake Ritsa">Lake Ritsa</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Abkhazia covers an area of about 8,660&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (3,344&#160;sq&#160;mi) at the western end of Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> to the north and the northeast divide Abkhazia and the Russian Federation. To the east and southeast, Abkhazia is bounded by the Georgian region of <a href="/wiki/Samegrelo-Zemo_Svaneti" title="Samegrelo-Zemo Svaneti">Samegrelo-Zemo Svaneti</a>; and on the south and southwest by the Black Sea.\n</p><p>Abkhazia is diverse geographically with lowlands stretching to the extremely mountainous north. The Greater Caucasus Mountain Range runs along the region\'s northern border, with its spurs&#160;&#8211;&#32;the Gagra, <a href="/wiki/Bzyb_Range" title="Bzyb Range">Bzyb</a> and Kodori ranges&#160;&#8211;&#32;dividing the area into a number of deep, well-watered valleys. The highest peaks of Abkhazia are in the northeast and east and several exceed 4,000 meters (13,123&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. Abkhazia\'s landscape ranges from coastal forests and citrus plantations to permanent snows and <a href="/wiki/Glaciers" class="mw-redirect" title="Glaciers">glaciers</a> in the north of the region. Although Abkhazia\'s complex topographic setting has spared most of the territory from significant human development, its cultivated fertile lands produce tea, tobacco, wine and fruits, a mainstay of the local agricultural sector.\n</p><p>Abkhazia is richly irrigated by small rivers originating in the Caucasus Mountains. Chief of these are: <a href="/wiki/Kodori_River" title="Kodori River">Kodori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bzyb_River" title="Bzyb River">Bzyb</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghalidzga_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ghalidzga River (page does not exist)">Ghalidzga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gumista_River" title="Gumista River">Gumista</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Psou_River" title="Psou River">Psou River</a> separates the region from Russia, and the <a href="/wiki/Inguri_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Inguri River">Inguri</a> serves as a boundary between Abkhazia and Georgia proper. There are several <a href="/wiki/Periglacial" class="mw-redirect" title="Periglacial">periglacial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crater_lake" title="Crater lake">crater</a> lakes in mountainous Abkhazia. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ritsa" title="Lake Ritsa">Lake Ritsa</a> is the most important of them.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg/220px-Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg/330px-Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg/440px-Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="487" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ridge_view_from_pitsunda_cape.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View from <a href="/wiki/Pitsunda" title="Pitsunda">Pitsunda</a> cape</div></div></div>\n<p>The world\'s deepest known cave, <a href="/wiki/Veryovkina_Cave" title="Veryovkina Cave">Veryovkina Cave</a>, is located in Abkhazia\'s western Caucasus mountains. The latest survey (as of March 2018) has measured the vertical extent of this cave system as 2,212 meters (7,257&#160;ft) between its highest and lowest explored points.\nBecause of Abkhazia\'s proximity to the Black Sea and the shield of the Caucasus Mountains, the region\'s climate is very mild. The coastal areas of the republic have a subtropical climate, where the average annual temperature in most regions is around 15&#160;\xc2\xb0C (59&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and the average January temperature remains above freezing.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The climate at higher elevations varies from maritime mountainous to cold and summerless. Also, due to its position on the windward slopes of the Caucasus, Abkhazia receives high amounts of <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">precipitation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> though humidity decreases further inland. The annual precipitation vacillates from 1,200\xe2\x80\x931,400&#160;mm (47.2\xe2\x80\x9355.1&#160;in)<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> along the coast 1,700\xe2\x80\x933,500&#160;mm (66.9\xe2\x80\x93137.8&#160;in) in the higher mountainous areas. The mountains of Abkhazia receive significant amounts of snow.\n</p><p>The lowland regions used to be covered by swaths of <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">beech</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hornbeam" title="Hornbeam">hornbeam</a>, which have since been cleared.<sup id="cite_ref-EB_4-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are two main entrances into Abkhazia. The southern entrance is at the <a href="/wiki/Inguri" class="mw-redirect" title="Inguri">Inguri</a> bridge, a short distance from the city of <a href="/wiki/Zugdidi" title="Zugdidi">Zugdidi</a>. The northern entrance ("Psou") is in the town of <a href="/wiki/Leselidze_(town)" title="Leselidze (town)">Leselidze</a>. Owing to the situation with a recognition controversy, many foreign governments advise their citizens against travelling to Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> According to President Raul Khajimba, over the summer of 2015, thousands of tourists visited Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_Abkhazia" title="Government of the Republic of Abkhazia">Government of the Republic of Abkhazia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Abkhazia" title="Politics of Abkhazia">Politics of Abkhazia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Abkhazia" title="Elections in Abkhazia">Elections in Abkhazia</a></div>\n<p>Abkhazia is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-presidential">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, and the second elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_Abkhazia" title="President of Abkhazia">President of Abkhazia</a> was <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bagapsh" title="Sergei Bagapsh">Sergei Bagapsh</a>. Bagapsh came to power following the deeply divisive <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Abkhazian presidential election, 2004">October 2004 presidential election</a>. The next election was held on 12 December 2009. Bagapsh was re-elected as president with 59.4% of the total vote.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Ankvab" title="Alexander Ankvab">Alexander Ankvab</a>, his vice president, was appointed acting president after the former president\'s death on 29 May 2011<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> until winning election in his own right later on <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_presidential_election,_2011" title="Abkhazian presidential election, 2011">26 August 2011</a>.\n</p><p>Legislative powers are vested in the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Assembly_of_Abkhazia" title="People&#39;s Assembly of Abkhazia">People\'s Assembly</a>, which consists of 35 elected members. The last <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_parliamentary_election,_2012" title="Abkhazian parliamentary election, 2012">parliamentary elections</a> were held on 10/24 March 2012. Ethnicities other than Abkhaz (Armenians, Russians and Georgians) are claimed to be under-represented in the Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-Today_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Today-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most refugees from the 1992\xe2\x80\x931993 war (mainly ethnic Georgians) have not been able to return and have thus been excluded from the political process.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Abkhazian officials have stated that they have given the Russian Federation the responsibility of representing their interests abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a 2010 study published by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Colorado_Boulder" title="University of Colorado Boulder">University of Colorado Boulder</a>, the vast majority of Abkhazia\'s population supports independence, while a smaller number is in favour of joining the Russian Federation. Support for a reunification with Georgia is very low.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Even among ethnic Georgians, nearly 50% prefer Abkhazia to remain an independent state and less than 20% of them believe returning to Georgia is necessary, as most of them have adjusted to the current situation. Among ethnic Abkhaz, explicit support for reunification with Georgia is around 1%; a similar figure can be found among ethnic Russians and Armenians as well.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_Republic_of_Abkhazia">Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Autonomous_Republic_of_Abkhazia" title="Government of the Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia">Government of the Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_of_Abkhazia.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Government_of_Abkhazia.svg/220px-Government_of_Abkhazia.svg.png" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Government_of_Abkhazia.svg/330px-Government_of_Abkhazia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Government_of_Abkhazia.svg/440px-Government_of_Abkhazia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="689" data-file-height="373" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_of_Abkhazia.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Autonomous_Republic_of_Abkhazia" title="Government of the Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia">Government of the Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Government of the Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia is the <a href="/wiki/Government_in_exile" title="Government in exile">government in exile</a> that Georgia recognises as the legal government of Abkhazia. This pro-Georgian government maintained a foothold on Abkhazian territory, in the upper <a href="/wiki/Kodori_Valley" title="Kodori Valley">Kodori Valley</a> from July 2006 until it was forced out by fighting in August 2008. This government is also partly responsible for the affairs of some 250,000 <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" class="mw-redirect" title="Internally displaced persons">IDPs</a>, forced to leave Abkhazia following the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992%E2%80%9393)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Abkhazia (1992\xe2\x80\x9393)">War in Abkhazia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Georgians_in_Abkhazia" title="Ethnic cleansing of Georgians in Abkhazia">ethnic cleansing</a> that followed.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The current Head of the Government is <a href="/wiki/Vakhtang_Kolbaia" title="Vakhtang Kolbaia">Vakhtang Kolbaia</a>.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992%E2%80%9393)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Abkhazia (1992\xe2\x80\x9393)">War in Abkhazia</a>, the Government of the Autonomous Republic of Abkhazia (at the time the Georgian faction of the "Council of Ministers of Abkhazia") left Abkhazia after the Abkhaz separatist forces took control of the region\xe2\x80\x99s capital <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">Sukhumi</a> and relocated to Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s capital <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a> where it operated as the Government of Abkhazia in exile for almost 13 years. During this period, the Government of Abkhazia in exile, led by <a href="/wiki/Tamaz_Nadareishvili" title="Tamaz Nadareishvili">Tamaz Nadareishvili</a>, was known for a hard-line stance towards the Abkhaz problem and frequently voiced their opinion that the solution to the conflict can be attained only through Georgia\'s military response to secessionism.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Later, Nadareishvili\'s administration was implicated in some internal controversies and had not taken an active part in the politics of Abkhazia<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> until a new chairman, <a href="/wiki/Irakli_Alasania" title="Irakli Alasania">Irakli Alasania</a>, was appointed by <a href="/wiki/President_of_Georgia" title="President of Georgia">President of Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a>, his envoy in the peace talks over Abkhazia.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Abkhazia" title="Subdivisions of Abkhazia">Subdivisions of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg/220px-Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg.png" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg/330px-Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg/440px-Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="313" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abkhazia_districts_map_numbered.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1) <a href="/wiki/Gagra_District" title="Gagra District">Gagra</a> 2) <a href="/wiki/Gudauta_District" title="Gudauta District">Gudauta</a> 3) <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi_District" title="Sukhumi District">Sukhumi</a> 4) <a href="/wiki/Gulripshi_District" title="Gulripshi District">Gulripshi</a> 5) <a href="/wiki/Ochamchira_District" title="Ochamchira District">Ochamchira</a> 6) <a href="/wiki/Tkvarcheli_District" title="Tkvarcheli District">Tkvarcheli</a> 7) <a href="/wiki/Gali_District,_Abkhazia" title="Gali District, Abkhazia">Gali</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Republic of Abkhazia is divided into seven <a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">raions</a> named after their primary cities: <a href="/wiki/Gagra_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Gagra district">Gagra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gudauta_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Gudauta district">Gudauta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Sukhumi district">Sukhumi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ochamchira_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Ochamchira district">Ochamchira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulripshi_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulripshi district">Gulripshi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tkvarcheli_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Tkvarcheli district">Tkvarcheli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gali_(town)" title="Gali (town)">Gali</a>. These districts remain mostly unchanged since the breakup of the Soviet Union, with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Tkvarcheli_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Tkvarcheli district">Tkvarcheli district</a>, created in 1995 from parts of the Ochamchira and Gali districts.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The President of the Republic appoints districts\' heads from those elected to the districts\' assemblies. There are elected village assemblies whose heads are appointed by the districts\' heads.<sup id="cite_ref-Today_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Today-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)#Regions,_republics,_and_districts" title="Georgia (country)">administrative subdivision of Abkhazia used by Georgia</a> is identical to the one outlined above, except for the new Tkvarcheli district.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Abkhazia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Abkhazia">Military of Abkhazia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_Air_Force" title="Abkhazian Air Force">Abkhazian Air Force</a></div>\n<p>The Abkhazian Armed Forces are the military of the Republic of Abkhazia. The basis of the Abkhazian armed forces was formed by the ethnically Abkhaz National Guard, which was established in early 1992. Most of their weapons come from the former Russian airborne division base in Gudauta.<sup id="cite_ref-Chervonnaia_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chervonnaia-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WhiteBookOfAbkhazia_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteBookOfAbkhazia-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> The Abkhazian military is primarily a ground force, but includes small sea and air units. Russia has at present around 1,600 troops stationed in Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Abkhazian Armed Forces are composed of:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The Abkhazian Land Forces with a permanent force of around 5,000, but with <a href="/wiki/Reservists" class="mw-redirect" title="Reservists">reservists</a> and paramilitary personnel this may increase to up to 50,000 in times of military conflict. The exact numbers and the type of equipment used remain unverifiable.</li>\n<li>The Abkhazian Navy that consists of three divisions based in <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">Sukhumi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ochamchire" title="Ochamchire">Ochamchire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pitsunda" title="Pitsunda">Pitsunda</a>, but the Russian coast guard patrols their waters.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_Air_Force" title="Abkhazian Air Force">Abkhazian Air Force</a>, a small unit consisting of a few <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">fighter aircraft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helicopters" class="mw-redirect" title="Helicopters">helicopters</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Abkhazia" title="Economy of Abkhazia">Economy of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<p>The economy of Abkhazia is heavily integrated with Russia and uses the <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> as its currency. Abkhazia has experienced a modest economic upswing since the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia war">2008 South Ossetia war</a> and Russia\'s subsequent recognition of Abkhazia\'s independence. About half of Abkhazia\'s state budget is financed with aid money from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tourism is a key industry and, according to Abkhazia\'s authorities, almost a million tourists (mainly from Russia) came to Abkhazia in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Abkhazia also enjoys fertile lands and an abundance of agricultural products, including tea, tobacco, wine and fruits (especially <a href="/wiki/Tangerine" title="Tangerine">tangerines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hazelnut" title="Hazelnut">hazelnuts</a>). Electricity is largely supplied by the <a href="/wiki/Inguri_Dam" class="mw-redirect" title="Inguri Dam">Inguri hydroelectric power station</a> located on the Inguri River between Abkhazia and Georgia (proper) and operated jointly by both parties.\n</p><p>In the first half of 2012, the principal trading partners of Abkhazia were Russia (64%) and Turkey (18%).<sup id="cite_ref-apress6859_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apress6859-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> economic sanctions imposed on Abkhazia in 1996 are still formally in force, but Russia announced on 6 March 2008 that it would no longer participate in them, declaring them "outdated, impeding the socio-economic development of the region, and causing unjustified hardship for the people of Abkhazia". Russia also called on other CIS members to undertake similar steps,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> but met with protests from Tbilisi and lack of support from the other CIS countries.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite the controversial status of the territory and its damaged infrastructure, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Abkhazia" title="Tourism in Abkhazia">tourism in Abkhazia</a> grew following the Russian recognition of Abkhazian independence in 2008 due to the arrival of Russian tourists. In 2009 the number of Russian tourists in Abkhazia increased by 20% and the total number of Russian tourists reached 1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Low prices and an absence of any visa requirements attracts Russian tourists especially those who cannot afford vacations in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and other popular Russian tourist destinations. After the tourist boom many Russian businesses began to invest money in Abkhazian tourist infrastructure. With the main highway of the country being rebuilt in 2014 many damaged hotels in Gagra are either being restored or demolished. In 2014, 1.16 million Russian tourists visited Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Abkhazia" title="Demographics of Abkhazia">Demographics of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<p>According to the last census in 2011 Abkhazia has 240,705 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The exact size of Abkhazia\'s population was unclear. According to the census carried out in 2003 it measured 215,972 people,<sup id="cite_ref-censuses_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censuses-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> but this is contested by Georgian authorities. The Department of Statistics of Georgia estimated Abkhazia\'s population to be approximately 179,000 in 2003, and 178,000 in 2005 (the last year when such estimates were published in Georgia).<sup id="cite_ref-yb2005_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yb2005-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica">Encyclop\xc3\xa6dia Britannica</a></i> estimates the population in 2007 at 180,000<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Crisis_Group" title="International Crisis Group">International Crisis Group</a> estimates Abkhazia\'s total population in 2006 to be between 157,000 and 190,000 (or between 180,000 and 220,000 as estimated by <a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a> in 1998).<sup id="cite_ref-Today_third_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Today_third-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The ethnic composition of Abkhazia has played a central role in the <a href="/wiki/Georgian-Abkhazian_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian-Abkhazian conflict">Georgian-Abkhazian conflict</a> and is equally contested. The demographics of Abkhazia were very strongly affected by the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Abkhazia_(1992%E2%80%931993)" title="War in Abkhazia (1992\xe2\x80\x931993)">1992\xe2\x80\x931993 War with Georgia</a>, which saw the expulsion and flight of over half of the republic\'s population, measuring 525,061 in the 1989 census.<sup id="cite_ref-censuses_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censuses-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The population of Abkhazia remains ethnically very diverse, even after the 1992\xe2\x80\x931993 War. At present the population of Abkhazia is mainly made up of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz people">Abkhaz</a> (50.8% according to the 2011 census), <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Mingrelians" title="Mingrelians">Mingrelians</a>), <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Abkhazia" title="Armenians in Abkhazia">Hemshin Armenians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>. Other ethnicities include <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gogia2011_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gogia2011-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greeks constituted a significant minority in the area in the early 1920s (50,000), and remained a major ethnic component until 1945 when they were deported to Central Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Under the Soviet Union, the Russian, Armenian, and Georgian populations grew faster than the Abkhaz population, due to large-scale enforced migration, especially under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lavrenty_Beria" class="mw-redirect" title="Lavrenty Beria">Lavrenty Beria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jrl_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jrl-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Russians moved into Abkhazia in great numbers.\n</p><p>At the time of the 1989 census, Abkhazia\'s Georgian population numbered 239,872 forming around 45.7% of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-censuses_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censuses-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Numbers2011_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Numbers2011-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> and the Armenian population numbered 77,000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Due to <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Georgians_in_Abkhazia" title="Ethnic cleansing of Georgians in Abkhazia">ethnic cleansing</a> and displacement due to people fleeing the 1992-1993 war, much of the Georgian population and to a lesser extent the Russian and Armenian populations had greatly diminished.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> In 2003 Armenians formed the second-largest minority group in Abkhazia (closely matching the Georgians), numbering 44,869.<sup id="cite_ref-censuses_199-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censuses-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> By the time of the 2011 census, <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a> formed the second-largest minority group with a number of 46,455.<sup id="cite_ref-Numbers2011_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Numbers2011-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Despite the official numbers, unofficial estimates believe that the Abkhaz and Armenian communities are roughly equal in number <sup id="cite_ref-oD_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oD-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a> Abkhazia granted refugee status to a few hundred Syrians with Abkhaz, <a href="/wiki/Abazin" class="mw-redirect" title="Abazin">Abazin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Circassians" title="Circassians">Circassian</a> ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-oD_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oD-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Facing a growing Armenian community, this move has been linked with the wish of the ruling Abkhaz \xe2\x80\x94who have often been in the minority on their territory\xe2\x80\x94 to tilt the demographic balance in favour of the titular nation.<sup id="cite_ref-oD_206-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oD-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">Diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Thousands of Abkhaz, known as <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Cleansing_of_Circassians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Cleansing of Circassians"><i>muhajirun</i></a>, fled Abkhazia for the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in the mid-19th century after resisting the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian</a> conquest of the Caucasus. Today, Turkey is home to the world\'s largest Abkhaz diaspora community. Size estimates vary \xe2\x80\x93 Diaspora leaders say 1 million people; Abkhaz estimates range from 150,000 to 500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Abkhazia" title="Religion in Abkhazia">Religion in Abkhazia</a></div>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:none"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Abkhazia (2003)<sup id="cite_ref-portal-credo_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portal-credo-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0
