colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_Native_Religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz Native Religion">Abkhaz Native Religion</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:Red; width:8%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">8%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other religions</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:DarkKhaki; width:2%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">Irreligious</a> or <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:Silver; width:8%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">8%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Undetermined</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:DarkGray; width:6%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">6%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Most inhabitants of Abkhazia are Christian (<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslim</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">irreligious</a>, but few people who declare themselves Christian or Muslim attend religious service.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_Native_Religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz Native Religion">Abkhaz Native Religion</a> has undergone a strong revival in recent decades.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> There is a very small number of adherents of Judaism, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_religious_movement" title="New religious movement">new religious movements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-portal-credo_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portal-credo-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The Jehovah\'s Witnesses organisation has officially been banned since 1995, though the decree is not currently enforced.<sup id="cite_ref-state_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the constitutions of both Abkhazia and Georgia, the adherents of all religions (as well as atheists) have equal rights before the law.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a survey held in 2003, 60% of respondents identified themselves as Christian, 16% as Muslim, 8% as atheist or irreligious, 8% as adhering to the traditional Abkhazian religion or as Pagan, 2% as follower of other religions and 6% as undecided.<sup id="cite_ref-portal-credo_209-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portal-credo-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Article 6 of the Constitution of Abkhazia states:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>The official language of the Republic of Abkhazia shall be the Abkhazian language. The Russian language, equally with the Abkhazian language, shall be recognized as a language of State and other institutions. The State shall guarantee the right to freely use the mother language for all the ethnic groups residing in Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>The languages spoken in Abkhazia are <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_language" title="Abkhaz language">Abkhaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mingrelian_language" title="Mingrelian language">Mingrelian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Svan_language" title="Svan language">Svan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenian (language)">Armenian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek (language)">Greek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>  The Autonomous Republic passed a law in 2007 defining the Abkhaz language as the only state language of Abkhazia.<sup id="cite_ref-OBC_transeuropa_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBC_transeuropa-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> As such, Abkhaz is the required language legislative and executive council debates (with translation from and to Russian) and at least half of the text of all magazines and newspapers must be in Abkhaz.<sup id="cite_ref-OBC_transeuropa_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBC_transeuropa-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite the official status of Abkhaz, the dominance of other languages within Abkhazia, especially Russian, is so great that experts as recently as 2004 called it an "<a href="/wiki/Endangered_language" title="Endangered language">endangered language</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Hewitt_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hewitt-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> During the Soviet era, language instruction would begin in schools in Abkhaz, only to switch to Russian for the majority of required schooling.<sup id="cite_ref-Hewitt_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hewitt-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The government of the Republic is attempting to institute Abkhaz-only primary education but there has been limited success due to a lack of facilities and educational materials.<sup id="cite_ref-OBC_transeuropa_216-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OBC_transeuropa-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>  Even in Georgian-speaking areas of the Republic, ending schooling in that language has resulted in teachers switching to Russian-language materials instead of Abkhaz-language teaching.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nationality_issues">Nationality issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Nationality issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Adoption_of_Russian_nationality">Adoption of Russian nationality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Adoption of Russian nationality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After the breakup of Soviet Union, many Abkhazians kept their <a href="/wiki/Soviet_passport" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet passport">Soviet passports</a>, even after a decade, and used them to eventually apply for Russian citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-Soviet_Abkhazians_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soviet_Abkhazians-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before 2002, Russian law allowed residents of former Soviet Union to apply for citizenship if they had not become citizens of their newly independent states. The procedure was extremely complex. The new <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_Russia" title="Citizenship of Russia">citizenship law of Russia</a> adopted on 31 May 2002 introduced a simplified procedure of citizenship acquisition for former citizens of the Soviet Union regardless of their place of residence. In Abkhazia and South Ossetia, the application process was simplified even further, and people could apply even without leaving their homes. Russian nationalist non-governmental organisations with close ties to Russian officialdom simply took their papers to a nearby Russian city for processing.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Abkhazians began mass acquisition of Russian passports in 2002. It is reported that the public organisation the Congress of Russian Communities of Abkhazia started collecting Abkhazians\xe2\x80\x99 Soviet-era travel documents. It then sent them to a consular department specially set up by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Foreign_Ministry" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Foreign Ministry">Russian Foreign Ministry</a> officials in the city of <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a>. After they were checked, Abkhazian applicants were granted Russian citizenship. By 25 June 2002, an estimated 150,000 people in Abkhazia had acquired the new passports, joining 50,000 who already possessed Russian citizenship. The Sukhum authorities, although officially not involved in the registration for Russian nationality process, openly encouraged it. Government officials said privately that President Putin\xe2\x80\x99s administration agreed with the passport acquisition during Abkhazia\xe2\x80\x99s prime minister <a href="/wiki/Anri_Jergenia" title="Anri Jergenia">Djergenia</a>\'s visit to Moscow in May 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Soviet_Abkhazians_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soviet_Abkhazians-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>"passportisation"</i> caused outrage in Tbilisi, worsening its already shaky relations with Russia. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_Georgia" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Georgia">Georgian Foreign Ministry</a> issued a statement insisting that Abkhazians were citizens of Georgia and calling the passport allocation an\n"unprecedented illegal campaign". President <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Shevardnadze" title="Eduard Shevardnadze">Eduard Shevardnadze</a> said that he would be asking his Russian counterpart, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, for an explanation. The speaker of parliament <a href="/wiki/Nino_Burjanadze" title="Nino Burjanadze">Nino Burjanadze</a> said that she would raise the matter at the forthcoming OSCE parliamentary assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-Soviet_Abkhazians_219-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soviet_Abkhazians-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>1 February 2011 was the last day in the post-Soviet era when a passport of <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a> was valid for crossing the Russian-Abkhaz border. According to the staff of Abkhazia\'s passport and visa service, there were about two to three thousand mostly elderly people left with Soviet passports who had no chance of acquiring new documents. These people were not able to get Russian citizenship. But they can first get an internal Abkhaz passport and then a travelling passport to visit Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Issue_of_ethnic_Georgians">Issue of ethnic Georgians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Issue of ethnic Georgians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2005, citing the need to integrate ethnic Georgian residents of eastern districts of Abkhazia, the then-leadership of Abkhazia showed signs of a softening stance towards granting of citizenship to the residents of Gali, Ochamchire and Tkvarcheli districts.<sup id="cite_ref-Abkhaz_Parliament_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abkhaz_Parliament-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the Abkhazian law on citizenship, <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abkhaz people">ethnic Abkhazians</a>, regardless of place of residence, can become Abkhaz citizens. Those who are not ethnic Abkhazians are eligible for citizenship if they lived in Abkhazia for at least five years prior to adoption of act of independence in October, 1999. This provision aimed at creating a legal hurdle in obtaining Abkhaz passports for those ethnic Georgians who fled Abkhazia as a result of 1992-1993 armed conflict and who then returned to the Gali district. Abkhazian legislation forbids citizens of Abkhazia from holding <a href="/wiki/Dual_citizenship" class="mw-redirect" title="Dual citizenship">dual citizenship</a> with any other state apart from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Abkhaz_Opposition_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abkhaz_Opposition-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ethnic Georgians who have returned to the Gali district and want to obtain Abkhaz passports, according to Abkhazian law, should undergo lengthy procedures which also include a requirement to submit documented proof that they renounced their Georgian citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-Abkhaz_Opposition_223-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abkhaz_Opposition-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> President Bagapsh was inclined to regard Georgians in Gali as "Georgianised Abkhazians." According to Bagapsh, these were actually ethnic Abkhaz people who were "Georgianised" during the long process of the Georgianisation of Abkhazia that culminated during the rule of Joseph Stalin and Lavrenti Beria. So in his official speeches, Bagapsh often added the Gali Georgians to population estimates of the Abkhaz, disregarding the fact that they still thought of themselves as ethnic Georgians rather than Abkhaz.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early 2013 the process of passportisation of ethnic Georgians came under the scrutiny of Abkhaz opposition groups who turned this issue into one of the central topics of the breakaway region\xe2\x80\x99s internal politics, and issuing of passports was suspended in May. Opposition claimed that "massive" passportisation involving granting citizenship to ethnic Georgians in eastern districts was fraught with risk of "losing sovereignty and territorial integrity." According to Apsnipress, <a href="/wiki/Stanislav_Lakoba" title="Stanislav Lakoba">Stanislav Lakoba</a>, secretary of Abkhaz security council, said that "We are facing the process of the total Georgianization of Abkhazia."<sup id="cite_ref-Abkhaz_Opposition_223-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abkhaz_Opposition-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Pressures have been placed upon teachers in areas of Abkhazia which retain large Georgian populations to abandon the use of the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian language</a> in education and adopt Russian textbooks.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 September 2013, the Parliament of Republic of Abkhazia adopted a resolution instructing the prosecutor\xe2\x80\x99s office to carry out a "sweeping" probe into passport offices of the interior ministry and where wrongdoings were found in the distribution of passports to refer those violations to the Ministry of Internal Affairs for "annulment of illegally issued passports." Abkhaz officials announced that a significant number of residents of Gali, Ochamchire and Tkvarcheli districts received Abkhaz passports while at the same time retaining their Georgian citizenship, which constituted a "violation of the law on Abkhaz citizenship". According to the Abkhaz officials, more than 26,000 passports were distributed in Gali, Tkvarcheli and Ochamchire districts, including about 23,000 of which were given out since Russian recognition of Abkhazia\'s independence in August, 2008. These political debates have caused concerns in the ethnic Georgian population of Abkhazia, who reside mainly in Gali district, that they would be stripped of Abkhazian citizenship and thus forced to leave Abkhazia again.<sup id="cite_ref-Abkhaz_Parliament_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abkhaz_Parliament-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2013 Alexander Ankvab signed a document ordering the firing Stanislav Lakoba. The document did not state any reason for the decision but Lakoba saw it as related to his political position on granting citizenship to Georgians living in Gali. Lakoba claimed that, according to data from the Abkhaz Security Council, 129 local people in Gali fought against Abkhazia. Local political parties and the coordination council of civil organisations expressed concern about Lakoba\xe2\x80\x99s dismissal. They claimed that, by dismissing him, the president "made an illegal process legal" \xe2\x80\x93 giving Abkhazian passports to Georgian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Abkhazia" title="Culture of Abkhazia">Culture of Abkhazia</a></div>\n<p>The written <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_language" title="Abkhaz language">Abkhaz</a> literature appeared relatively recently, in the beginning of the 20th century. However, Abkhaz share the <a href="/wiki/Nart_saga" title="Nart saga">Nart sagas</a>, a series of tales about mythical heroes, with other Caucasian peoples. The <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_alphabet" title="Abkhaz alphabet">Abkhaz alphabet</a> was created in the 19th century. The first newspaper in Abkhaz, called <i>Abkhazia</i> and edited by <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Gulia" title="Dmitry Gulia">Dmitry Gulia</a>, appeared in 1917.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Arguably the most famous Abkhaz writers are <a href="/wiki/Fazil_Iskander" title="Fazil Iskander">Fazil Iskander</a>, who wrote mostly in Russian, and <a href="/wiki/Bagrat_Shinkuba" title="Bagrat Shinkuba">Bagrat Shinkuba</a>, a poet.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> remains the most popular <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Abkhazia" title="Sport in Abkhazia">sport in Abkhazia</a>. Other popular sports include basketball, boxing and wrestling.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> National Basketball Team of Abkhazia played its first game with the Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus Basketball team on 27 May 2015, which Abkhaz team won by 76-59.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Abkhaz basketball team "Apsny" also plays in the Russian Basketball League\'s Third-Tier in Krasnodar Krai.\n</p><p>Abkhazia has had its own amateur Abkhazian football league since 1994 though it has no international football union membership.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 2016 it hosted and won the <a href="/wiki/ConIFA_World_Football_Cup" title="ConIFA World Football Cup">ConIFA World Football Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Abkhazia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" a disputed territory</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
